#  [](/thread/161278-directional-movement)Directional Movement

  * [#1](/thread/161278-directional-movement "Post Permalink")

  * [ ACartwright](acartwright)

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=63488)

Hi Everyone,  
  
I have been trying for the last 4-5 years to find the perfect system.  
  
That is the perfect system for me - every trader has his/her own special way of trading or analysing the same peice of information.  
  
I want to trade on 1 hr charts as I work from home and I want to be able to decide whether to excute a trade quickly.  
  
I can do this with this system in about a minute befroe the new candle opens.  
  
I have tried using just price action and also every indicator ever coded but there are two indicators that I keep coming back to.  
  
I have gone back over the last year on G/J and I have an 80% success rate.   
  
I have concluded on average that in a normal week there will be 5 trades - 4 will win or break even and one will be an outright loser.  
  
The avergae loser will be 50 to 60 pips.  
  
This means as long as I lock in 60 pips per week I should not have negative week on average.  
  
Indicators will follow.  
  
This is a screen shot of the places where I executed trades for the week.  
  
The buy and sell happened at the close of these candles.  
  
I do not have a solid exit as yet - I simply use the average approach - so any comments are welcome for this.  
  
In the chart 6 trades I made ended up making a profit (or breaking even) whilst one was a simple loser.  
  
Can anyone guess which 2 indicators I used?  
  
I will post them if anyone shows and interest.  
  
I look forward to peoples thoughts.  
  
Al

The settings for the indicator can remain the same.

  * [#10](/thread/post/2644494#post2644494 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 2, 2009 12:14am  Apr 2, 2009 12:14am 

  * [ ACartwright](acartwright)

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=63488)

Rules:  
  
The rules are as follows:  
  
Buy  
  
Buy when the following occurs.  
  
1\. +DMI is greater than the -DMI -The +DMI has to be greater than a level of 20  
2\. The ADX has risen since the last bar and is over 20. The only time you can trade when the ADX is under 20 is if it has moved 3 points of it's low  
3\. No trades when ADX above 40  
4\. MACD agrees with the move - i.e. MACD is above signal line.  
  
Sell  
  
Sell when the following occurs.  
  
1\. -DMI is greater than the +DMI -The -DMI has to be greater than a level of 20  
2\. The ADX has risen since the last bar and is over 20. The only time you can trade when the ADX is under 20 is if it has moved 3 points off it's low  
3\. No trades when ADX above 40  
4\. MACD agrees with the move - i.e. MACD is above signal line.  
  
Exit - I normally use standard s/r or movement in the DMI.  
  
Stop loss - Low/High of indicating candle + spread  
  
Get to break even around 30 - 40 pips.  
  
Like I said this has a good win/loss ratio.

  * [#13](/thread/post/2644525#post2644525 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 2, 2009 12:29am  Apr 2, 2009 12:29am 

  * [ ACartwright](acartwright)

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=63488)

Rules:  
  
Sorry people I forgot an important item on entry.  
  
MACD is only used as a confirmation indicator.  
  
If the MACD is not correct at the time you get a signal of DMI/ADX you should leave the trade alone completely until the next set up on DMI.  
  
It is tempting to go in after MACD is correct also but in the long run more trades will fail.

In conjunction they compliment each other really well.

I prefer to use this on hourly charts.  
  
This is due to wanting maybe 1 to 2 trades a day.  
  
This strategy also works on lower time frames with the same sort of % success rate but you iwll have to change your take profit/break even part of the strategy.  
  
You will probably get 4-5 trades as result of reducing the time frame.

  * [#31](/thread/post/2647728#post2647728 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 3, 2009 1:16am  Apr 3, 2009 1:16am 

  * [ ACartwright](acartwright)

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=63488)

Hi guys,  
  
These are the cad/jpy trades for this week.  
  
5 trades so far - 2 outright losers.  
  
However the other 3 have made some pretty good gains.  
  
It is also good to look at basic candlstick formations with this system.  
  
This is due to the DMI taking the highs and lows into account and cannot necessarily distinguish candlestick patterns.  
  
A candlestick showing a hammer could be shown on the DMI as a good candle - i.e. on a down trend it may have a lower low and a lower high. However it is still hammer and any trade should be taken with caution.  
  
Especially if it is this candle that causes the ADX to rise.  
  
Hope that makes sense.

Hi Billbss,  
  
Glad you had some success.  
  
I have posted the usd/chf trade that you may have taken.  
  
It is worth noting that if you got in at the right time your position should have been up 33 pips (not inc spread).   
  
As this pair does not move as much as some others I would say to have gone to break even after 25-30 pips.  
  
Also the indicating candle was rather a large one and these trades are prone to some form of pull back.  
  
As for candlesticks and tea leaves - well some people like them and some dont.  
  
The good thing about this strategy is the if you get a signal after a large run down it may be best to stay out and play another day.  
  
Just like the large indicating candle scenario.

  * [#35](/thread/post/2647937#post2647937 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 3, 2009 2:47am  Apr 3, 2009 2:47am 

  * [ ACartwright](acartwright)

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=63488)

Hi guys,  
  
This is an exit I have been using.  
  
The exit strategy relates to the histogram made by the macd and it's signal line.  
  
i.e. difference between the two.  
  
When there is a down movement (long) or an up movement (short) in the histogram place your take profits on the low of the corresponding candle.  
  
I have attached a screenshot.  
  
This signals that a reversal (or temporary pull back) is on the cards.  
  
This movment normally proceedes a downturn in the ADX - so when you should be getting out of a trade anyway.  
  
But it is normally one candle quicker which is always a good thing.  
  
Hope it helps. 

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: eur-usd - 1h 30.03.2009 to 02.04.2009.gif
Size: 49 KB](/attachment/image/227972/thumbnail?d=1365567021)](/attachment/image/227972?d=1238697915)   

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#36](/thread/post/2647980#post2647980 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 3, 2009 3:06am  Apr 3, 2009 3:06am 

  * [ ACartwright](acartwright)

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=63488)

Just to add to the exit strategy.  
  
If you do not get taken out on the low of the indicating candle and MACD histogram makes another low simply move the take profit up to the low o fthe next candle and keeping doing so until it is hit.  
  
You may find the histogram starts to widen again.  
  
Simply follow the same process as before.  
  
Hope thats clear as mud.

> For a long position do u wait for both lines to cross above on the MACD histogram or just the yellow? and vice versa for a short
> 
> Ignored

Hi Pipping,  
  
The MACD has to be above signal for long and below for short.  
  
The histogram will be positive for long and negative for short.  
  
I do not take into account if MACD line is above/below the zero line.  
  
Hope that answered your question.

> Disliked
> 
> To ACartwright:

>  Did you ever think about turning this indicator into an expert advisor ? Pretty straightforward entry and exit criteria's make this an excellent candidate for an EA. Just thinking of people that would like to trade your system but do not have the time to watch the markets during the day.  
>    
>  Let me know your thoughts.
> 
> Ignored

Hi Caputoe,  
  
I have thought about turing this into an ea but have not done so for a couple of reasons:  
  
1\. I trade this manually - like I said on previous posts I look at the charts at 10 minutes before the hour ends and then I place my trade dependent on the criteria.  
2\. I use a combination of exit strategies that coud be hard to program into an EA. These include standard s/r and pivot points. However that being said the use of MACD or DMI could potentially be programmed.  
3\. Sometimes I exit on a potential candlestick pattern (Billbss will like this! - lol!)  
  
If you want to start to look at this as an option please feel free to do so.  
  
I started this thread as none of the other discussions looked at the DMI.  
  
I wanted people to see that when it is used with another trend indicator how effective it could be.  
  
DMI has been a favourite of mine since the start.  
  
Hiope that answers your question.

Thanks for posting the details of your system, ACartwright.  
  
  
I haven't seen anything so far about the initial stop placement, or movement of stops as the trade progresses.  
  
  
I am making the logical assumption of placing the initial stop behind the latest swing high/low. (See the attached chart)  
  
  
I understand your exit rule "When there is a down movement (long) or an up movement (short) in the histogram place your take profits on the low of the corresponding candle."   
  
  
In the mean time it might be wise to trail the stop behind 2 or 3 closed bars to guard against any explosive move against your position while waiting for the exit condition to occur.  
  
  
What do you think?  
  
  
By the way, I am (temporarily) in profit 103 pips on that trade as I write. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1)

Hi Dave,  
  
The exit strategy is a little rough as I do not have any hard and fast rules. I simply move my position on feeling.  
  
Often I reduce the stop in line with the following candles high/lows and try to get to b/e when it is possible (without compromising my position.  
  
As for the initial stop loss this can be either be in relation to the last swing high/low or I use the high/low of the indicating candle.  
  
In theory a downtrend is a series of lower highs and lower lows - a stop should not be hit when you are in the trend - I do however leave a little room just in case of the pip hunters.  
  
I am glad that you have had early success so far and look forward to your commetns going forward.

Hi there,  
  
In answer to your questions:  
  
1\. Once trade is up 30-40 pips try to move stop loss to b/e.  
2\. Stoploss goes on high of indicating candle for short and low of indcating candle for long.  
3\. I have been playing around with the DMI for around 4 years and have demoed using confirming indicators. The MACD is the best one I have found.  
  
Hope that helps.

I had a profitable day yesterday. For someone with experience with this system it could have been great.  
  
Here is a short entry on the USDJPY today about an hour before the London session open. It looks a little risky sitting right on top of S1, but it did break through later, so it may work out. We will see.  
  
I'm attaching a "MTF_MACD_inColor" indicator I'm using that makes it easier to see when the MACD histogram is above or below the zero line. It's the same as the standard one except it colors the histo bars as they appear above or below. It doesn't change the system any, it just makes it easier on the eyes.

Hi Dave,  
  
Thanks for posting that indi - hopefully it will allow other to clearly see when MACD confirms.  
  
I am glad that you had a profitable day yesterday and hope that you locked some profit.  
  
In reference to s/r pivot points I have noticed that this system does not really take much notice of the support and resistance. This is due to it being more on momentum - i.e. rising adx showing momentum in price.  
  
What I do look out for is price action s/r. This is a lot more signifcant and often use it come out of positions.

  * Apr 9, 2009 12:37am  Apr 9, 2009 12:37am 

  * [ ACartwright](acartwright)

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=63488)

> [Quoting Bobcat2](/thread/post/2658360#post2658360 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Sorry if this has been answered before, but I don't understand what you mean by "3 points off its low". Please elaborate and thanks.
> 
> Ignored

Hi bobcat,  
  
To answer your question.  
  
3 off its low means that you can trade if the adx is below 20.  
  
As long as it has moved 3 off of its low point.  
  
Ie.  
  
ADX goes from 15.8 to 17.4 to 19.1 - the 19.1 candle becomes the signal candle and a trade should be executed in the direction of the DMI.  
  
Likewise the adx can go 18.2 to 20.2 - this then is a trade straightaway on the 20.2 candle as adx is now over 20.  
  
HOpe that makes sense. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

> [Quoting sholmes9000](/thread/post/2658387#post2658387 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked

> hi acartwright....just wondering for instance, say there's a bullish crossover (+dmi>-dmi and +dmi>20), macd also above signal. and adx fell initially say from 31 to 29 but then later at end of next bar, it jumps up to 30....do we still take the long trade (even if adx is trading in the highs of 20s or in the region of 30s)? tks.
> 
> Ignored

Hi sholmes,  
  
Yes that would be a trade as adx has risen.  
  
You have to be careful with these trades as the adx has a finite way to travel.  
  
In theory adx travelling from a lower level has a "potential" to travel further.  
  
Hope that helps.

  * [#99](/thread/post/2659084#post2659084 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 9, 2009 2:05am  Apr 9, 2009 2:05am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar18160_4.gif) deltaworld](deltaworld)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: 3 Year NooB | [148 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=18160)

I used my platform's assisted programming to write a program to illustrate and follow the rules by your system. I'm not a programmer but if there is a programmer there that can use this or possibly write a an ea for it then I hope this should help. I have also backtested this system over the last 3 months and it came with a profit where setting this on a 40 pip stop loss MAX and exit on MACD crossing. with a 1% of capital management on lot size.  
  
The script below is only for long's but I guess this could also be done for SHORT's  
  
The system I used is IT-finance ProBuilder  
  
REM Buy  
  
indicator1 = DIplus[14](close)  
indicator2 = DIminus[14](close)  
c1 = (indicator1 > indicator2)  
  
indicator3 = ADX[14]  
c2 = (indicator3 > 20.0)  
  
indicator4 = ADX[14]  
c3 = (indicator4 < 40.0)  
  
indicator5 = MACDline[12,26,9](close)  
indicator6 = ExponentialAverage[9](MACDline[12,26,9](close))  
c4 = (indicator5 > indicator6)  
  
IF c1 AND c2 AND c3 AND c4 THEN  
BUY 1 %CAPITAL AT MARKET THISBARONCLOSE  
ENDIF  
  
  
REM Sell  
  
indicator7 = MACDline[12,26,9](close)  
indicator8 = ExponentialAverage[9](MACDline[12,26,9](close))  
c5 = (indicator7 <= indicator8)  
  
IF c5 THEN  
SELL AT MARKET THISBARONCLOSE  
ENDIF 

_______________ Say Good-bye to Buy-and-Hold

> hi acartwright, yes your usdcad attachment reflects the similar situation which i encountered. i did take the trade but it a an emotional ride as price came just 2 pips off my stop before recovering to enable me to take a modest 30 pips profit. was trading euro.

>  also would like your advice say if there's a bearish crossover, +dmi is 15, -dmi is 25 but adx declined say from 20 to 19 but at end of next bar adx went up from 19 to 21.5 but -dmi has shrunk from -25 to -23 while +dmi from 15 to 13. with the -dmi value declining from -25 to -23, is...
> 
> Ignored

I would always wait until I got a +DMI reading over 20 for long and -DMI reading over 20 for short.  
  
When DMI is below 20 the price action is often choppy.  
  
Also when DMI goes above and then below 20 you should be tightening stops.

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=63488)

> [Quoting sholmes9000](/thread/post/2660171#post2660171 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> ok, so as long as +dmi or -dmi stays above 20, we can still take trade even if +dmi/-dmi values have decreased from prev bar. tks
> 
> Ignored

When you get a decrease in DMI it simply means that the current bar failed to make a higher highs or lower lows. OR it has made a higher high or a lower low but not in proportion with the last candles low/high.  
  
Hope that makes sense.  
  
Sometimes the changes in DMI reflect swing highs and swing lows.  
  
Clear as mud?

>  1.3315 entry & after that, it made low at 1.3277....still awaiting trade to develop.

> Ignored

I have just looked at the trade you have taken and it is a valid trade based on the criteria.  
  
I mentioned in the early posts that you have to be careful with the signal candles.  
  
This includes the actual size of the candle.  
  
The indicating candle in this instance had a range of 62 pips - which is quite large for an hourly eur/usd bar.  
  
With such large bars it is likely that there is a retracement.  
  
In this case there was a pull back but your original stop should not have been hit until you were at least 20 pips in profit.  
  
At this point with this type of trade it may have been best to move to breakeven as the trend had temporarily ceased as per the "rounding off" of the macd and the +DMI falling back to the 20 area.  
  
On the flip side - the stop loss has not yet been hit - the lows have become static at 13275 - it might be best to keep the original stop loss in place.  
  
Hope that helps.

Hi Delta,  
  
Moving to b/e after 40 pips is normally a good move on the more volatile pairs - not necessarily the yen pairs as usd/jpy an chf/jpy do not move as much as pound/yen eur/yen etc.  
  
I also sometimes take profit after 40 pips if price has hit s/r for example or it looks like the trade wil lturn back.  
  
I have also exited after 40 pips if I am down for the day if it brings me to break even for the day.  
  
So all in all there are a lot of factors involved.  
  
What I like about these two indicators is that they based on different inputs.  
  
MACD is based on closing prices and DMI is the high/lows and net directional movement.  
  
Also in regard to your eur/yen trade you have to be careful of large candles that become signal candles - pound/yen eur/yen I would not enter on a cnadle that showed a signal if its range was say over 100 pips.  
  
You could be putting your self in a compromised position resulting in a pull back.  
  
Hope that the above helps.

Hi ACartWright  
  
I have posted the chart for the BE trade for Eur/JPY  
  
1\. There was a big candle that was validated by the strategy   
2\. Entry SHORT at 131.508 at close of indicating Candle  
3\. Stop Loss Initially set to High + Spread of Indicating Candle  
4\. The Price moves to 131.045 setting the trade to +42.3 Pip  
5\. The SL is now moved to BE  
6\. Price Action moves and bounces back up to BE and the trade is closed at 0pips  
  
P.S. I have since monitored the pair since posting the chart and the price is now 131.218 and would have been +25pips had the SL not moved to BE.  
  
Any suggestions on how to manage the movement of the Stop Loss from its initial point to BE on this trade or other similar trades?

Hi Delta,  
  
It is a tricky thing to move stop losses to break even at the correct time.  
  
I think it is best to look at the indicators overall and when the price gets to break even.  
  
I.E if it gets to break even at the end of the candle you can look at what the indicators are suggesting.  
  
If it is at the beginning you may want to lock in straightaway and hope for a continued move.  
  
The exit is always the problem as you will never know how far price will go.  
  
In an ideal world I would close 50% of the trade off when a s/r target is made and then move to b/e on the rest.  
  
Unfortunately I am in the process of building my account so I take profit as and when.  
  
Sorry to be so vague.  
  
I have attached a chart to try and explain.

Hi Henry,  
  
I have only looked at possible trades on the 4hr charts not taken any live.  
  
The reason for this is based on the system the sl goes at low/high of indicating candle. 4H candles can be very large.  
  
Also I have settled on the 1 hour charts as they often provide regular (not too many) singals which means if you miss one you can get on the next.  
  
This strategy works on any time frame and on any pair but as I mentioned in earlier post b/e and tp have to be adjusted accordingly.

Hi Delta,  
  
It is not really ideal to get in late.  
  
usd/cad had moved 100 pips from the low of the day so there was always a potential pull back on the horizon.  
  
This strategy is designed to get you in as quick as posibble and to b/e as soon as possible.  
  
Then giving you the freedom to tp at s/r levels or whenever you choose.  
  
I would say to stay out of a trade if you have missed the original signal.  
  
If you do ge tin late the sl shoudl be on the indicating candle low/high which at that point could be a few pips away.

  * [#161](/thread/post/2671575#post2671575 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 16, 2009 3:35am  Apr 16, 2009 3:35am 

  * [ ACartwright](acartwright)

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=63488)

> [Quoting thehenryfam](/thread/post/2671478#post2671478 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> AC, is this something that must always be considered before taking a trade, i.e. that a candle in the opposite direction may have been what caused the ADX to tick up? If that is the case, do you leave such trades alone? The G/U trade worked out ok for me (took profit on one position and B/E on second), but I just wanted to know going forward.  
>    
>  Cheers,  
>  Scott
> 
> Ignored

Hi Scott,  
  
Its a good question.  
  
In my opinion if a down candle has a high higher and a higher low in an uptrend it is still a valid signal - (obviously reverse in down trend).  
  
This is because this is what defines a trend.  
  
I normally put the stop loss in the same position. i.e. low or high of indicating candle but often look to see if the low or high has come back to a s/r line. I then put my stop there.  
  
These normally result in a high reward to risk.  
  
If the down candle is one of the candlestick formations (hammer or hanging man) I sometimes wait for the break of the high or low for entry.  
  
Hope that helps.  
  
With so many pairs you can be very selective.

  * [#164](/thread/post/2671935#post2671935 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 6:46am  Apr 16, 2009 6:27am | Edited 6:46am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar18160_4.gif) deltaworld](deltaworld)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: 3 Year NooB | [148 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=18160)

**Parabolic SAR Stop Loss Strategy**  
  
I have been doing a lot of backtesting on previous trades that I have entered live or demo traded that I have either exited the trade at Break Even or I have exited the trade at a loss and looking at ways of fine tuning these trades to maximise profits and at the same time minimise the exposure to risk over time.  
  
I have toyed with the use of Parabolic SAR before and have used it as exit strategies but this indicator as shown in the many diagrams that I have below becomes very effective with a trending pair. The Parabolic SAR becomes ineffective when there is no trend. So tie this in with the use of this strategy and the ADX indicator with the +DI and -DI then you have a winning formula.  
  
The default values for the Parabolic SAR work fine but these may need to be fined tuned, depending on the TF you are using and the pair that you are using, but in most cases the default values work. The default settings of Parabolic SAR are:  
  
Minimum Acceleration: **0.02**  
Acceleration Step: **0.02**  
Maximum Acceleration: **0.2**  
  
Let me clarify, I'll walk you through each of the charts to explain fully.  
  
**CADJPY Chart**  
As you can see there is a rising trend and you would have got into it about half way with this indicator. With the original stop loss method on my demo trade I was stopped out at the candle indicated. Instead if a Parabolic SAR was setup then you can move the stop loss with the SAR and you would have stayed in the trade and have a larger profit margin.  
  
**EURAUD Chart**  
Another Example as above, in my demo trade I got stopped out early, with SAR I would have stayed in. and there was a further move down. Even using a standard trend line you can see that one of the candles had opened outside of the trend line drawn but yet it still moved down, with the SAR in place it kept us in the trade.  
  
**EURJPY Chart**  
There are 2 arrows here  
**Arrow 1:** In Arrow one you can see that this is where I had exited a live trade at Break-Even. With Parabolic SAR the trade would still be in and you would have gained a great drop in price action, as indicating by the large candle formation straight after I was stopped out.  
  
**Arrow 2:** This is where Parabolic is not perfect and the settings mentioned above can be fined tuned for the pair as the Parabolic SAR got us out early when the down trend had remained. But it is always better to be safe than sorry.  
  
**USDCAD Chart**  
In this example I was in a live trade but I got stopped out early with a -pips, again with the use of SAR I can see that I would have still been in the trade but a strong support has formed round about point of entry and the bottom wicks of the candles have lined up. This gives me a strong indication to get out at the bottom wick of the current candle, which would have been Break Even or a 2-5 pips in profit depending on entry and risk take.  
  
**EURGBP Chart**  
Now in this chart, The Parabolic doesn't work in our favour and keeps us in a trade that is now moving sideways, whilst with the original stop loss method we would have gotten out earlier. There are two ways we can manage this.  
  
**1.** The first way, is when we do realise that we are in a sideways moving pair we can determine the support and resistance of the moving channel and exit the trade (on a SHORT) at the bottom wicks of the candles to maximise profit  
  
**2.** Using other indicators and other methods to determine end of trend or reversal. 

  1. **A** : ADX Breakout: We can see that I have drawn a red trend line just below the smooth up trending ADX we can see that this has broken on the following candle which is an indicator to get out.
  2. **B** : Courtesy of CobraForex I have the THVTrix 4.0 indicator which is a very useful indicator and the fast trix as you can see has turned green which is an indication that it the trend has ended or is due to reverse.
  3. **C** : THV RSI V2, courtesy of the THV team. (or any RSI indicator will do) again we have an RSI breakout and this is another indication that the trend has broken from the red trend line that I have drawn on the RSI

  
**GBPJPY**  
If you notice the downtrend in this trade. I had entered a live trade on this account and thank god for the effective Stop Loss management because about an hour into the trade, the pair had suddenly reversed and I was stopped out with a -36 pip loss. Which I understand, you can't win them all.  
Now if I had used the Parabolic SAR technique I would have suffered a -28 pip loss, not much in it, but what I am trying to show here, is that the use of the Parabolic is not riskier than the original technique.  
If you have noticed a trend reversal due to fundamental's or was expecting one from another strategy or indicator.. then this is a point where you can SAR (Stop And Reverse) and where you exited the trade, if you had entered the trade as a LONG.. you would have profited from a trending range and have many pips in your account.   
  
Of course, there is a more of a risk element here as the Parabolic Stops are more distant from entry and price than the previous technique but as the name suggests Parabolic, is that they do tighten up as the trend runs out of steam, If used effectively I believe that this can definately maximise your profits but at the same time keep the losses to a minimum.  
  
I have yet to test this with hard fact figures, but from what I have seen on previous trades, this would have been a winner.  
  
Again, comments or suggestions or even ideas on how this can be improved would be great.

Hi Delta,  
  
I am currently in a chf/jpy trade which is +32.  
  
I put the stop loss slightly higher than the indicating candles high so am fortunate to be still in it.  
  
As for some comments to your last post I would never consider trading outside London session and on the hours where New York is ending it's day.  
  
The reason is that it goes very flat.  
  
ADX DMI and MACD can be affected by very small candles as a result.  
  
I would stick to London session as this is where "the money" trades. Moves are bigger which means we can get to break even asap.  
  
This will stop you potentially overtrading and buying into false moves.  
  
In repsonse to news events you are never going to have a trade where there is no news announced.  
  
What you need to be careful of is major news and understand how any "good" or "bad" news will affect the trade.  
  
Also you will never know when a big institution will cash a cheque in foreign courrency for a few billion - all affecting price.  
  
In regard to coming out of a trade early - well exiting a trade is the hardest thing of all.  
  
You never know when price will retrace or do you?  
  
I try to get to b/e when it is sensible to do so - this would be when the indicators are still confirming the move up or down whether it is mid candle or at the end.  
  
I will then look for notable s/r and draw a line on my chart.  
  
I TP when this line is hit.  
  
Before I look at a trade I look at the s/r and see if I can get to b/e with say 30 - 40 pips in the bag.  
  
Hope those comments help.

Well done on both of those trades, congratulations  
  
In regards to me LONG on chf/jpy, I had read this article  
[http://www.dailyfx.com/story/trading...816684913.html](http://www.dailyfx.com/story/trading_reports/pairs_to_range_trade/CHFJPY_Offers_A_Stable_Range_1239816684913.html)  
  
I normally don't trust trade signals or reviews like these, but I believed that one, and did my own analysis and the review made sense so i entered a stop order to go long.  
  
In hinesight, I can see what i should have done: After being stopped out the AUD/USD with a loss, I should have researched what news release had caused this at the time the stop loss was hit.  
  
Then I would have made a judgement on the impact of this news release on the currencies as a whole (I'm not very good at judging how much the news impacts what currencies). But obviously this news release has had such a big impact on the asian/australasian currencies that I should have cancelled the stop order on the CHF/JPY.  
  
I guess for next time, If I get stopped (when I shouldnt have) due to a sudden release.  
1\. Find out why? Fundamental? News Release?  
2\. Study the impact this would have on the currencies  
3\. If there is an impact on orders to open currencies.  
4\. Delete Any orders that may be affected by the news release.  
  
I guess that is the key to using Fundamental & Technical Analysis.  
  
This has been a very expensive week for me. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f641.png?v=15.1)

I've set the Stop Loss to the Parabolic SAR at the 30min set at

  * [#182](/thread/post/2674069#post2674069 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 17, 2009 1:43am  Apr 17, 2009 1:43am 

  * [ ACartwright](acartwright)

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=63488)

Hi Delta,  
  
I don't think over the long run that the SAR will provide good exit points.  
  
The problem with any indicator and this includes MACD and DMI is that they lag.  
  
It is normally good to use them to get in but getting out you need something twice as dynamic.  
  
Saying that I still like using th MACD histogram as this show the convergence of 2 emas.  
  
I still think the best way is to plot s/r (including use of trenlines) reversal points because price action is the quickest indicator.  
  
Also use pivot points.  
  
I hope that you bagged a few pips from the eur/aud trade. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#183](/thread/post/2674135#post2674135 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 17, 2009 2:09am  Apr 17, 2009 2:09am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar18160_4.gif) deltaworld](deltaworld)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: 3 Year NooB | [148 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=18160)

Still in the trade!!! at +40 pips  
  
The Parabolic SAR is there only to keep you in the trade for as long as possible and is there just to protect you from any sudden movements in the markets or sudden sentiment change, it's like an insurance blanket.  
  
From analysing trends, they either suddenly change and reverse, or they run out of steam.  
  
With the trends that run out of steam the Para SAR is your friend as it stays with you till the trend goes flat, but with sudden sentiment change, not so much but it does protect you from sudden drops but at the same time iron out any minor retracements to the overall trend.  
  
From looking at trends, most trends actually run out of steam, in regards to maximising the profit margin for sudden changes then you need a leading indicator, there is not that many about and reading them is not that easy as some of them are inauspicous. One that I have found easy to read is the Trix, as soon as the Fast trix changes to red then it may be a sign to get out.  
  
I have set the TP point to 161.8% Fib retracement of high-low of last down trend. which is calculated at 18732.1  
  
(see attached)  
  
Another way is reading divergences in the RSI, this is a good article  
<http://www.guppytraders.com/gup342.shtml>  
as with these signals it can get you out of trouble before it happens.

Yes I am using your exit strategies exactly as you had mentioned on the live account for 10 trades whilst testing the other method on demo.  
  
The exit I am using is set to: (on live)  
1\. Stop Loss to High+Spread of signal Candle  
2\. TP to 1st s/r  
3\. When +40pip, set to B/E  
4\. Move SL to High of Candle with a receding MACD Histo.

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: 3 Year NooB | [148 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=18160)

I closed on the demo, as the exit strategy is if any one of the 3 methods show a signal.. you get out.  
  
3 signals are:  
1\. Fast trix turns Green  
2\. ADX breaks trend line  
3\. RSI breaks trend line  
  
The CHF/JPY signalled from exit number 1.  
But then it signalled the other 2 as well but I had exited the trade by then.  
The Fast trix is a leading indicator and can get you out of sharp reversal trends.. This trend just ran out of steam.  
  
  
details below:  

1: 17/4/08 S.CHF/JPY SAR (30min 0.15, 0.07, 0.08)

Enter: 8616.9  

+61.9 Live: Exit 1st TP: 8555 +61.9

+118.4 Demo: Exit Fast Trix Green: 8498.5

  * [#216](/thread/post/2679060#post2679060 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 20, 2009 4:13am  Apr 20, 2009 4:13am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar18160_4.gif) deltaworld](deltaworld)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: 3 Year NooB | [148 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=18160)

I have been thinking of another way of maximising the profits on a longer term trend.  
  
Let's say we get a signal on a currency, and we enter as a trend is happening on the 1h hour chart. We are in the trade and the trade is going well, we then look at the 2hour chart and we notice that we are also within the confines of a valid trade adx>20 +di>-di and +di>20 for long. and macd is valid too for the 2h.   
  
My question is: As we are in the trade on the 1h could we use this to scale our trade to the 2h and as long as we set our stops at minimum of break-even but this gives us the potential for trends that carry through on the 2h scale, we could carry this through to 4h, and 1 day and scale our trades accordingly.  
  
And I guess to determine the exit, we can also scale down in the opposite direction if we notice a reverse in price action we can then have a look from 1d to 4h if price is shifting and look down in further detail.  
  
This is an idea and i'm only thinking out of the box and I don't know if this would actually work in practice.  
  
After I conclude the current test I am doing with the possible SAR and 3 different signals on exit for maximising profits, I might have a look at this one later.  
  
I have also decided that 10 trades is a bit short sighted in regards to the effectiveness of the SAR/3 Exit strategy and will trial this out till the end of this week (with a minimum of 10 trades) and post the outcome here to see what the result difference is.

  * [ volvo40](volvo40)

hi to maximise the returns for any trade you are looking for whats not possible only the big few who control the whole thing can tell you that the market manipulators: but for us mere mortals try using bollinger bands and the williams ind its like rsi but faster it depends on your time frame but basically using candles in an uptrend away from the lower band when a candle spike touchesor goes near a band and as it does the williams reverses then get out it wont work for anything over an hourly chart cos you have to sit there and watch it looking for that sudden spike but for skimmers its ideal especially when the bollinger is in a channel and your just running side to side but you should never trade against the longer term trend i.e if youir using 5min charts and the hourly says up wait for the bounceoff alower band with the williams or rsi in same direction as the bounce and in till williams bounces off a resistance and out simple skimming parabolic sars are good for bounces as well especially when they are inside the bolliger band you have to look at the overall picture of a chart whats in the way of the next target will it get past thats where the williams comes in it weakens out for now dont see the profit go

  * [#226](/thread/post/2680579#post2680579 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 6:31pm  Apr 20, 2009 6:14pm | Edited 6:31pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar18160_4.gif) deltaworld](deltaworld)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: 3 Year NooB | [148 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=18160)

> [Quoting oblo](/thread/post/2680452#post2680452 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> As per the rules I entered this trade and out for few pips because of the two long preceding candles and worried of retracement.
> 
> Ignored

I've been looking at a way of strategizing a technique for setting the breakeven dependant on the volatility of the pair, as each pair reacts differently.  
  
With the indicator attached, this calculates the ATR (Average Trading Range) and x 3 then it gives you a figure of recommended Stop Loss.  
  
From looking at past trades and with high volitility pairs e.g. eur/jpy and gbp/jpy they may need to have a higher b/e trading range.  
  
=(ATR*3)/Factor gives you the recommended B/E point.  
Where Factor is 2.948113208  
e.g.  
  
for AUD/USD Indicator shows 75 for ATR*3  
75/Factor = 25.5 pip till B/E  
  
A few more examples  
EURJPY  
125/Factor= 42.4 pip till B/E  
  
NZDUSD  
66/Factor= 22.4 pip till B/E  
  
GBP/JPY  
171/Factor= 58 pip till B/E  
  
USD/JPY  
75/Factor= 25.2 pip till B/E  
  
Now the reasoning behind dividing by this factor is that from looking at previous trades (especially the more volatile ones) setting at 40 pips b/e might occasionally get you stopped out at B/e when the trend continues down again on a minor retracement due to volatility of the pair.  
  
But, if you want to be extra conservative and stick to the original 20-40 b/e pip rule, then a minimum and maximum can be set. e.g. A minimum b/e even pip point will never be less than 20 and maximum b/e pip is 40.  
  
I hope this is helpful.  
  
This would then make the b/e rule easier to program if needed for automation through an EA. This will then be scalable to any timeframe and any currency. This will also scale to the current conditions affected by the average trading range e.g. news/other currency movmenents/stock movements/etc etc.  
  
p.s. I received another valid signal for EUR/JPY which was entered at 12770 for a target of 12700  
  
AUD/USD was closed for a +30pip 

Attached File(s)

Here are some useful indicators.  
  
Fxsnipers adx - Adx line changes colour to indicate slope.  
  
Adx bars - colours your bars when adx and dminus dplus above 20.  
  
Adx signal - gives alert when di/dp crosses adx (its useful although entry using this ac's method usually comes in 1 hour before).

  * [#248](/thread/post/2682006#post2682006 "Post Permalink")

I had a look at eurchf too and I could see that the were was a valid entry point (shown as purple line for signal) then the reentry will happen on open of next candle (shown as red arrow).   
  
This would have netted you a -24.1 pip loss (inclusive of spread).  
Waited for retracement to complete and another signal to re-occur and enter on open of candle after signal (as shown).  
  
The TP level would be set at either of RSI trend line breaking (as you have shown) OR. at Strong Support (shown in yellow) from previous trend lows.. and this was also a larger time frame key fib level of 0.5  
  
TP at that level would have netted you +49 pip (inclusive of spread)  
  
A total balance of trading that pair for the day would have given you a +24.9 pip win.

Hi guys,  
  
After yesterdays big moves I would be selective in which trades you take as there is likely to be some retracement.  
  
Sometimes retracements after big moves causes the system to give signals - as they are defining a trend agianst the overall trend.  
  
It would be prudent if any trades are taken that they are watched closely and profits locked in at every opportunity.

#  [](/thread/161278-directional-movement)Directional Movement 

  * 

  * [#261](/thread/post/2683701#post2683701 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 21, 2009 7:07pm  Apr 21, 2009 7:07pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar18160_4.gif) deltaworld](deltaworld)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: 3 Year NooB | [148 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=18160)

There is very little directionality in the market today, the market not sure which way to go.   
  
So, as this strategy is called "Directional Movement" I'll probably stay out until I see a trend in at least one of the pairs.  
  
There is a strategy somewhere here on FF about correlation with pairs and when you spot a trend with one pair, is an early sign of a trend on another pair.   
  
Again, look out for a developing trend on any pair, even if you miss out on that one, its an early bird indication of a trend yet to come.  
  
IMHO: I think the trend is bearish on majors GU EU EJ but the market is just having a breather before further drops come along.  
  
It's also best to trade on the 1H with the direction of the longer term trend in progress or developing, rather than against it as this then increases your % wins. 

_______________ Say Good-bye to Buy-and-Hold

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#262](/thread/post/2683744#post2683744 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 8:26pm  Apr 21, 2009 7:31pm | Edited 8:26pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar18160_4.gif) deltaworld](deltaworld)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: 3 Year NooB | [148 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=18160)

Hi AC  
  
I have a question in regards to the rules of the strategy.  
  
Say you have entered a trade as was indicated by the signal candle and you have set your SL and your TP to 1st s/r. (as shown on diagram).  
  
But then the PA has decided to reverse on the direction that you were taking and it looks like it is to hit the SL that was set.  
  
We can see on the chart that the Histogram is narrowing, and is showing signs of reversal. And the +DI, and -DI are also showing signs of reversal.  
  
As you had mentioned before that when the trade is in profit and the histograms start receding then set the SL to the H/L of that candle, to lock in profits on a tighter stop. But in this case we are still at -pip and there is no room to lock in profits but we are seeing the histo start to recede.  
  
Another situation is: we are not in profit on the trade and the PA is between entry and SL and at least one of the following has occurred.  
  
1\. Histo has reversed  
2\. MACD has reversed  
3\. DI has reversed.  
  
A Do you then exit the trade at a smaller loss than if the PA had hit SL  
OR  
B Let the price continue, allowing it to maneuver between Entry and SL to then continue towards it's initial trend direction from the signal provided? and keeping the SL there to minimise any further losses.  
  
  
Thanks in advance  
Tareq

Hi Tareq,  
  
Good questions.  
  
My own style would be very similar to answer A. Take a smaller loss as the sl is now reduced.  
  
But sometimes dependent on how small /bigthe loss would be I would keep the original stop loss.  
  
If say the sl was moved to take a smaller loss but it was onyl say 5-10 pips away from the original I would keep the original one in place.  
  
If the move of the SL saved me +30 pips (of potnetial loss) I would ignore the first SL and move it accordingly.  
  
Hope that makes sense.

If all or one of the indcators started to go against me I would move my stop loss to the low of this candle.  
  
If by moving the stop loss it only moved the stop loss by 10 pips I would keep the SL in the orignal place.  
  
If the move was greater than 10 pips I would then move the sl to the low of the canlde that showed a potential reversal.  
  
The histogram shows a narrowing of the emas well before the DMI.  
  
However by placing a stop above this candle it is pretty much around the same level as the original stop loss.  
  
I would hterfroe not move the SL.

Hi delta,  
  
Hope I was clear in my description.  
  
Just going forward.  
  
1\. A trade can be taken late (with caution) if the signal candle had all indicators confirming at the same time.  
2\. A trade is not to be taken when the correctly positioned DMI/ADX is waiting for the MACD to confirm. If the MACD does not confirm at the same time wait for the next signal given by DMI/ADX.  
  
gbp/jpy is a great one to be on currently.

There was a signal on e/u at 0600 GMT - I entered on the close of this candle (i.e. start of 0700 GMT)  
  
Sometimes I start the day a little later - I just then wait for the signals from there.  
  
I would be cautious of joining a trade that had already moved a good distance.  
  
i.e. if at 0700 GMT the e/u had already moved 300 pips in the early hours even if the indis remained good I would be a little wary.  
  
I always try to get in on the trade at earliest possible stage as from this point b/e can happen a lot quicker.  
  
On the g/u there was divergence on the -DMI. - DMI was not getting greater whilst price was making new lows.

> 
> Disliked
> 
> hi acartwright....i entered a long in euro at 1.3077 as +dmi (up from 19.7 to 24) is greater than -dmi & adx rose from prev 28 to 28.3...watching stop 1 pip below low at 1.3048. is this entry correct? tks

> Ignored

Hi Sholmes  
  
At the brown line indicated is the signal, normally you would place the stop at the low of the signal candle +/- spread  
  
The low of the signal candle on my chart says 1.30477 but looking at that candle it does not have a wick and entry is so close to stop that it doesn't give the pair to breathe. So taking the previous candle's wick low at 1.30355 and I have a 2pip spread on my a/c so  
I would set the stop to 1.30335  
  
As soon as you are +31.6 pips then set it to b/e  
  
(This is my personal opinion, I may be wrong.)  
  
I hope this helps

>  As soon as you are +31.6 pips then set it to b/e  
>    
>  (This is my personal opinion, I may be wrong.)  
>    
>  I hope this helps
> 
> Ignored

yes s/r is a good place to get out of trade at the moment /$ is at resistance of 13135 which it reached and is now consolidating at that point..   
  
Or you can trail stop loss and leave it running. I had a position with nzd/usd last week that was on an uptrend but it was getting late and I needed to go to bed it was already on b/e so I just set it on trailing stop and in the morning I had closed the position with a +62 pip gain. if you have time to monitor it, a FF trader on this thread had a great exit strategy, so simple on the MA at 8 candles and if it closes twice consecutively below then you get out, but whatever you feel is appropriate.

Hi SHolmes. The exit strategy relating to 8MA is the one attached here from CanuckCT, which he demonstrated on eur/jpy (chart shown). This I have quickly back tested this on a few trends and when you have long trends it can keep you in them to the very end, but when there are quick reversal you may be caught out, especially on news releases or big sudden changes in market sentiment.

In 13076 and SL 13045.

It is the ADX that needs to rise 3 off bottom and not necessarily the DMI.

  * Apr 29, 2009 2:40am  Apr 29, 2009 2:40am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar50431_6.gif) CanuckCT](canuckct)

  * Joined Oct 2007 | Status: Summer is the best time of year! | [1,284 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=50431)

Exactly Delta....the use of the 8SMA is when you catch a trade that starts to trend.  
  
It's one way to keep you in a trade that really starts to move in your favor. The way I use it is if there are 2 consecutive candles that close on the other side of the 8SMA, you close the trade. So basically you check it every couple of hours when price is near the moving average..  
  
The other thing I look at is significant points of support and resistance using H4 and up and the hourly MACD cross.  
  
Cheers  
CanuckCT

Hi Holmes,  
  
I would sya yes you can still take the trade in this instance.  
  
When this happens be careful however and look for any s/r that could hinder the trade.  
  
Note - ADX moving from 30 upwards has less room to move than say ADX rising from 20.  
  
Hope that helps.

Hi Balle,  
  
3 off the bottom means that you can take a trade when ADX is not over 20 as long as it has increased by 3.  
  
I.E. ADX 12.4 to 14.6 to 15.6 would be a valid signal on ADX.

Hi Sholmes,  
  
Looks like a a good trade well taken.  
  
The good thing about the adx in this instance is that it has made a nice round bottom.  
  
Also MACD is moving well away from it's signal line.  
  
These trades can be high reward to low risk due to the nature of the signal candle. This one was a hammer but it had made a lower low and a lower high so no reason not to take it.  
  
It would be wary of any s/r however.

> hi acartwright....in one trade 2 weeks earlier, used the entry bar low minus 1 pip as stop for a buy entry, +1.2959, stop 1.2920. however, was stopped out as price traded to a low exactly at stop level, 1.2920 & then it reversed to trade higher.   
>  in your opinion, how do you re-enter long again? or do we just sit out altogether & wait for next signal? tks.

> Ignored

Hi Holmes,  
  
In answer to your question I would wait for another valid signal before I would enter again.  
  
Also in regard to stops it is always good to look at other s/r as potential stop points as long as they are int he vacinity of the low of the indicating candle.

  * May 12, 2009 4:19am  May 12, 2009 4:19am 

  * [ ACartwright](acartwright)

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=63488)

> [Quoting sholmes9000](/thread/post/2726150#post2726150 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> 1 hr euro, just went short at 1.3590 with stop at 1.3607. adx rose to 28.5 from 27.9 & macd below signal. but price action has gone really quiet....
> 
> Ignored

Hi holmes,  
  
This was a viald signal and you should not be in too much trouble with it.  
  
The only thing that I can add for futre is that you are now trading outside the London session.  
  
Euro and GBP pairs tend to lose their volatility after 5pm GMT.  
  
Most of the moves happen when the London session is alive.  
  
Also price has just moved thorugha round number.  
  
If I were you I would set your trade to b/e as there is support at 13575 ish.

>  The only thing that I can add for futre is that you are now trading outside the London session.  
>    
>  Euro and GBP pairs tend to lose their volatility after 5pm GMT.  
>    
>  Most of the moves happen when the London session is alive.  
>    
>  Also price has just moved thorugha round number.  
>    
>  If I were you I would set your trade to b/e as there is support at 13575 ish.
> 
> Ignored

ok got it....tks.  
yes not much volatility as you said....got out b/e in the end.  
and looks like eur 1 hr signalling long soon....  
+dmi>-dmi, adx also increasing from prev bar, macd just above signal....

  * [#357](/thread/post/2728568#post2728568 "Post Permalink")

  * May 12, 2009 11:32pm  May 12, 2009 11:32pm 

  * [ ACartwright](acartwright)

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=63488)

> [Quoting sholmes9000](/thread/post/2728171#post2728171 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> hi acartwright, on macd, are there any specific things to take note of? like bullish crossover when below zero line & bullish crossover when above zero line? is there any significance from your experience?   
>    
>  say when macd crosses signal line up from below & both are below zero line and quite far away from zero line, the trend tend to be stronger? as compared to a bullish crossover just below zero line?   
>    
>  tks....
> 
> Ignored

Hi holmes,  
  
There are no real specific things on the MACD that I can mention apart from the normal way to trade MACD.  
  
In this strategy it is only a confirming indicator.  
  
I would point out the following though:  
  
1\. MACD above signal line and above zero - strong upward potential  
2\. MACD above signal line and below zero - upward potential but could be a pull back - I normally check price action to see if it has strong upward potential or if it is going sideways.  
3\. MACD below signal line and below zero - strong downward potential  
4\. MACD below signal line and above zero - possible sideways or retracement. Look at PA to confirm.  
  
Hope that helps. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

Hi Canuck,  
  
Well I cannot tell you off if you make a profit now can I ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1).  
  
I try to trade when all 3 line up - this is just for being in a comfort zone.  
  
I can then tell myself if I have a loser that I traded on the best set up.  
  
If I go in late and do not stay with the strategy rules and lose it would be a case of well what if.  
  
I think the more you get used to the signals from the DMI you can go in one bar later if MACD then confirms or one bar earlier if the MACD is close to a cross.  
  
This is due to the DMI providing the more concrete signal.  
  
What I would try to do is probably get to break even slightly earlier in the move if I am taking the signal a bar late.  
  
As long as MACD is pointing in the correct direction I do not think it is too much of an issue - all the cross is is a cross past a 9 MA signal line.  
  
Obviuosly what you have done with this trade works out so congrats.  
  
Al

hi acartwright, just a general question.  
in trying to access whether price has any potential move upward/downward or going sideways, what can one look at (indicators?)? how do you normally access such situations? by looking at pure price action?  
tks....[/quote]  
  
Hi homes,  
  
Good question.  
  
The reason we trade a rise in the adx over 20 or 3 off its bottom is to make sure we are going with the overall direction.  
  
Normally if price is going sideways adx will be flat, under 20 or decreasing from a high level.  
  
ADX and DMI is based on directional movement from bar to bar.  
  
You can always draw a few trendlines through swing lows and highs also to get an overall picture. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#370](/thread/post/2734056#post2734056 "Post Permalink")

  * May 14, 2009 8:39pm  May 14, 2009 8:39pm 

  * [ ACartwright](acartwright)

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=63488)

> [Quoting sholmes9000](/thread/post/2733554#post2733554 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> hi acartwright, just need your opinion....  
>  when trading gbp/usd, shld we also apply indicating bar hi/lo as stops? or shld one use swing hi/lo as stops? cos thot that gbp/usd is quite volatile & better to use a bigger buffer for stops? tks....
> 
> Ignored

Hi holmes,  
  
You can put your stops where you feel comfortable.  
  
I place them at the high or low of the indicating candle. A trend is determined by lower lows and lower highs for short and vice versa for long.  
  
If you place your stop at the high or low in theory you should not be stopped out if you have entered on a trend.  
  
Hope that makes sense but it is really down to you. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [ sholmes9000](sholmes9000)

  * | Joined Mar 2009  | Status: Trader | [87 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=98152)

> [Quoting ACartwright](/thread/post/2734056#post2734056 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi holmes,  
>    
>  You can put your stops where you feel comfortable.  
>    
>  I place them at the high or low of the indicating candle. A trend is determined by lower lows and lower highs for short and vice versa for long.  
>    
>  If you place your stop at the high or low in theory you should not be stopped out if you have entered on a trend.  
>    
>  Hope that makes sense but it is really down to you.
> 
> Ignored

ok tks....

hi acartwright....just a question. when there's dmi crossover, do we need to observe the 'extreme point rule'? tks.... 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#373](/thread/post/2737640#post2737640 "Post Permalink")

  * May 16, 2009 12:54am  May 16, 2009 12:54am 

  * [ ACartwright](acartwright)

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=63488)

Hi holmes,  
  
The extreme point rule is kind of disregarded as 99% of the time with a rising adx the price goes past the extreme point of the dmi cross.  
  
Wilder introduced this for those persons just trading the dmi cross to cut down on whip saws. ADX was alter added.  
  
If you want to include it in this strategy please do so. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#381](/thread/post/2743197#post2743197 "Post Permalink")

  * May 20, 2009 1:52am  May 20, 2009 1:52am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar50431_6.gif) CanuckCT](canuckct)

  * Joined Oct 2007 | Status: Summer is the best time of year! | [1,284 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=50431)

I have an indicator for this method...it's still a bit rough, but identifies most of the trades.  
  
I post it here so that someone may help to finish it.  
  
The indicator draws a line on the bar after the trade triggers and a price tag for the open of that bar. It has the rule per AC, except for the 3 off the bottom where ADX is below 20. So look at the bar prior to the vertical line...that is where the trigger was met.  
  
Any and all comments are welcome.  
  
Thanks,  
CanuckCT

Hi Iamfx,  
  
Thnaks for you post.  
  
Yes I am still currently trading this method but the interest in the thread has died down a little so I have not posted for a while.  
  
I have been constnaly refinign the system to make sure I trade the very best of set ups.  
  
I will have a look at your MACD settings to see how well they work.  
  
In addition I have been thinking to myself why are some moves bigger than others.  
  
After a lot of manual backtesting I believe the best set ups occur when price has broken out of s/r or trendlines.  
  
The ADX if in the correct position adds to the move as the breakout is also a strong directional move also.  
  
I have pretty much cancelled the signals where the trade onyl moves a few pips.  
  
Try drawing trendlines and you will see when you get a signal from the system the move is larger than a non breakout.  
  
Hope that makes sense. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

> [Quoting Iamfx](/thread/post/2769395#post2769395 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Forgot to add--has anyone noticed that the signal is more reliable when the adx turns up from close to the baseline?
> 
> Ignored

This is true but you have to remember that the indicator follows price and not the other way around.  
  
A large move on the ADX is only so due to the large move in price.  
  
When we can identify a strong breakout in price this means that the ADX will travel further.  
  
If in a range and the price is near a resistance point there will only be a small movement in the adx.  
  
What we are trying to do is to trade a breakout which has directional movement behind it (i.e dmi correct and ADX increasing).  
  
This is in contrast to trading a spike going thorugh a resistance point with no strength.  
  
Hope that helps.

You are correct some retracement are good winners.  
  
This is also the reason why I use MACD crossing signal line without worying to much if the cross was above or below zero.  
  
What you need to look for in any direction is if price has broken through any s/r. This often leads to a larger move.  
  
If price has not broken through look to see where possible reversals will be.  
  
You can then calcualte your risk to potential win.

It seems the macd line being above the zero line denotes a good solid long trend and vise versa. The zero line seems to act as a 50 ma. The signal and macd line seem to act as a 10 and 20 ma.  
  

> [Quoting ACartwright](/thread/post/2648077#post2648077 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi Pipping,  
>    
>  The MACD has to be above signal for long and below for short.  
>    
>  The histogram will be positive for long and negative for short.  
>    
>  I do not take into account if MACD line is above/below the zero line.  
>    
>  Hope that answered your question.
